- [CD4-positive exhausted alpha-beta T cell](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_0020030) [definition](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/IAO_0000115) "A CD4-positive alpha-beta T cell that displays impaired function and altered differentiation as a result of chronic antigenic stimulation (e.g., chronic infection, tumors, or persistent inflammation). This state is characterised by sustained expression of PD-1 as a shared feature. Additional exhaustion-associated molecules, including the transcription factor TOX, and context- or stage-dependent changes in markers such as LAG-3, TIM-3, CD39, and T-bet, may also be observed; however, the expression levels of these molecules vary depending on exhaustion stage and tissue environment."^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string)

- [CD8-positive exhausted alpha-beta T cell](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_0020031) [definition](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/IAO_0000115) "A CD8-positive alpha-beta T cell that displays impaired function and altered differentiation as a result of chronic antigenic stimulation (e.g., chronic infection, tumours, or persistent inflammation). This state is characterised by sustained expression of PD-1 as a shared feature. Additional exhaustion-associated molecules, including expression of the transcription factor TOX and reduced T-bet, and context- or stage-dependent changes in markers such as LAG-3, TIM-3, CD39, and EOMES, may also be observed; however, the expression levels of these molecules vary depending on exhaustion stage and disease context."^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string)

### Dogiel type II neuron `http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_0020045`

#### Added
- Class: [Dogiel type II neuron](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_0020045) 

- [Dogiel type II neuron](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_0020045) [IAO_0000233](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/IAO_0000233) [3471](https://github.com/obophenotype/cell-ontology/issues/3471) 

- [Dogiel type II neuron](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_0020045) [creator](http://purl.org/dc/terms/creator) "GitHub Copilot"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

- [Dogiel type II neuron](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_0020045) [date](http://purl.org/dc/terms/date) "2026-03-10T14:42:58Z"^^[dateTime](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#dateTime) 

- [Dogiel type II neuron](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_0020045) [id](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#id) "CL:0020045"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

- [Dogiel type II neuron](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_0020045) [definition](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/IAO_0000115) "A neuron characterised by Dogiel type II morphology: a large, smooth, oval soma bearing multiple long axon-like processes (multiaxonal) that extend without branching until they reach their targets. The soma lacks the short lamellar or spiny dendrites characteristic of Dogiel type I neurons. Dogiel type II neurons were first described by Alexander Dogiel in 1899 based on methylene blue staining in gastrointestinal ganglia. In the enteric nervous system, Dogiel type II neurons correspond to intrinsic primary afferent neurons (IPANs) and exhibit AH-type electrophysiology (prolonged afterhyperpolarization following an action potential)."^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 
  - [database_cross_reference](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref) "PMID:34170401"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

- [Dogiel type II neuron](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_0020045) [has_exact_synonym](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasExactSynonym) "multiaxonal enteric neuron"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 
  - [database_cross_reference](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref) "PMID:34170401"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

- [Dogiel type II neuron](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_0020045) [has_exact_synonym](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasExactSynonym) "type II enteric neuron"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 
  - [database_cross_reference](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref) "PMID:34170401"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

- [Dogiel type II neuron](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_0020045) [has_related_synonym](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasRelatedSynonym) "AH neuron"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 
  - [database_cross_reference](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref) "PMID:34170401"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

  - [has_synonym_type](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasSynonymType) [OMO_0003000](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/OMO_0003000)

  - [database_cross_reference](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref) "PMID:34170401"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

- [Dogiel type II neuron of myenteric plexus](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_0020054) [has_exact_synonym](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasExactSynonym) "type II myenteric neuron"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 
  - [database_cross_reference](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref) "PMID:34170401"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

- [Dogiel type II neuron of myenteric plexus](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_0020054) [definition](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/IAO_0000115) "An intrinsic primary afferent neuron of the myenteric plexus characterised by Dogiel type II morphology: a large, smooth, oval soma bearing multiple long axon-like processes that extend without branching until they reach their targets in both the myenteric and submucosal plexuses and the mucosa. The soma lacks the dendrites characteristic of Dogiel type I neurons and is larger in cross-sectional area than either motor neuron type. This neuron is immunopositive for choline acetyltransferase (ChAT) and immunonegative for neuronal nitric oxide synthase (NOS1). It exhibits AH-type electrophysiology, characterised by a prolonged afterhyperpolarization (AHP) following an action potential. Substance P (encoded by TAC1) expression has been reported in subsets across species."^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 
  - [database_cross_reference](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref) "PMID:34170401"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

  - [database_cross_reference](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref) "PMID:40954253"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

  - [database_cross_reference](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref) "PMID:37355216"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

- [Dogiel type II neuron of myenteric plexus](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_0020054) [label](http://www.w3.org/2000/01/rdf-schema#label) "Dogiel type II neuron of myenteric plexus"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

- [Dogiel type II neuron of myenteric plexus](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_0020054) SubClassOf [Dogiel type II neuron](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_0020045) 

- [Dogiel type II neuron of myenteric plexus](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_0020054) SubClassOf [intrinsic primary afferent neuron of myenteric plexus](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_0020046)

It shows short-latency, non-direction-selective responses with large receptive fields and a distinctive rapid action potential waveform. In mammals it forms about five percent of RGCs and includes four conserved ON and OFF sustained and transient subtypes."^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string)

- [calcified zone articular chondrocyte](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_0020040) [id](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#id) "CL:0020040"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

- [calcified zone articular chondrocyte](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_0020040) [definition](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/IAO_0000115) "An articular chondrocyte located in the calcified cartilage zone below the tidemark at the interface between articular cartilage and subchondral bone, embedded within a mineralized extracellular matrix. In humans, this cell exhibits a hypertrophic-like phenotype and typically expresses collagen type X (COL10A1). Together with the surrounding calcified matrix, it forms a transitional region that mechanically couples the deep articular cartilage to the underlying subchondral bone."^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string)

  - [database_cross_reference](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref) "PMID:18455690"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string)

- [cervical dorsal root ganglion CGRP neuron](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4079000) [definition](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/IAO_0000115) "A peptidergic nociceptor whose soma is located in the cervical dorsal root ganglion, characterized by expression of calcitonin gene-related peptide (CGRP, encoded by CALCA). This small- to medium-diameter neuron belongs to the TrkA-positive peptidergic subpopulation and typically co-expresses substance P. It innervates peripheral tissues including skin and viscera, where it mediates neurogenic inflammation and nociceptive signalling through release of CGRP from peripheral terminals during tissue injury (Haberberger et al. 2019, PMID:31293388). In human DRG, CGRP-immunoreactive neurons represent a substantial proportion of nociceptors, comparable to the pattern observed in rodents (Rostock et al. 2018, PMID:29229553)."^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string)

- [cervical dorsal root ganglion Nav1.7 neuron](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4079002) [contributor](http://purl.org/dc/terms/contributor) [0000-0001-6677-8489](https://orcid.org/0000-0001-6677-8489) 

- [cervical dorsal root ganglion Nav1.7 neuron](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4079002) [date](http://purl.org/dc/terms/date) "2026-03-13T11:13:54Z"^^[dateTime](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#dateTime) 

- [cervical dorsal root ganglion Nav1.7 neuron](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4079002) [id](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#id) "CL:4079002"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

- [cervical dorsal root ganglion Nav1.7 neuron](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4079002) [definition](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/IAO_0000115) "A nociceptor whose soma is located in the cervical dorsal root ganglion and that expresses the voltage-gated sodium channel Nav1.7 (encoded by SCN9A). This neuron is characterized by Nav1.7-dependent action potential initiation and amplification, which is essential for normal pain sensation in humans. Nav1.7 contributes approximately 50% of total sodium channel current in human DRG nociceptors (Chang et al. 2018, PMID:28424991). In human DRG, Nav1.7 immunoreactivity is detected in 54-57% of TrkA-positive neurons (Rostock et al. 2018, PMID:29229553). Human genetic evidence confirms Nav1.7 as necessary and sufficient for nociceptive function in these neurons."^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string)

- [cervical dorsal root ganglion Nav1.9 neuron](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4079003) [definition](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/IAO_0000115) "A nociceptor whose soma is located in the cervical dorsal root ganglion and that expresses the voltage-gated sodium channel Nav1.9 (encoded by SCN11A). This neuron is characterized by a persistent, tetrodotoxin-resistant sodium current that modulates resting membrane potential and amplifies subthreshold depolarizations, contributing to enhanced excitability during inflammation (Dib-Hajj et al. 2002, PMID:11972962). In human DRG, Nav1.9-immunoreactive neurons constitute approximately 26% of TrkA-positive neurons, a significantly higher proportion than the 12% observed in mouse (Rostock et al. 2018, PMID:29229553), suggesting species differences in inflammatory pain processing."^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string)

- [cervical dorsal root ganglion Piezo2 neuron](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4079005) [definition](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/IAO_0000115) "A mechanosensitive sensory neuron whose soma is located in the cervical dorsal root ganglion and that expresses the mechanically activated ion channel Piezo2 (encoded by PIEZO2). This neuron transduces mechanical stimuli and is involved in light touch perception and proprioception. In human DRG, Piezo2-immunoreactive neurons constitute approximately 35% of TrkA-positive neurons, compared to 26% in mouse (Rostock et al. 2018, PMID:29229553). This subpopulation includes both low-threshold mechanoreceptors mediating innocuous touch and a subset of mechanically sensitive nociceptors, reflecting the dual role of Piezo2 in somatosensation across species."^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string)

This neuron is distinguished from peptidergic nociceptors by its dependence on glial cell-derived neurotrophic factor family ligands rather than nerve growth factor, and in rodents it characteristically binds isolectin B4. In human DRG, RET-immunoreactive neurons constitute approximately 46% of TrkA-positive neurons, a significantly higher proportion than the 23% observed in mouse (Rostock et al. 2018, PMID:29229553), indicating an expanded non-peptidergic nociceptor compartment in humans."^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string)

- [cervical dorsal root ganglion TRPV1 neuron](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4079008) [definition](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/IAO_0000115) "A polymodal nociceptor whose soma is located in the cervical dorsal root ganglion and that expresses the transient receptor potential vanilloid 1 channel (TRPV1, encoded by TRPV1). This neuron detects noxious heat above 43 degrees Celsius, protons, and endogenous lipid mediators, and is activated by capsaicin. In human DRG, TRPV1-immunoreactive neurons constitute approximately 54% of TrkA-positive neurons, significantly higher than the 35% observed in mouse (Rostock et al. 2018, PMID:29229553). These neurons are predominantly small-diameter nociceptors that innervate skin and visceral organs, where they function as primary detectors of thermal and chemical noxious stimuli."^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string)

- [cervical dorsal root ganglion endothelin-1 neuron](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4079001) [has_exact_synonym](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasExactSynonym) "cervical dorsal root ganglion Endothelin 1 neuron"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string)

- [cervical dorsal root ganglion endothelin-1 neuron](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4079001) [id](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#id) "CL:4079001"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

- [cervical dorsal root ganglion endothelin-1 neuron](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4079001) [definition](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/IAO_0000115) "A sensory neuron whose soma is located in the cervical dorsal root ganglion and that expresses endothelin-1 (EDN1). In rat DRG, EDN1 immunoreactivity has been detected in a subset of neuron somata (Giaid et al. 1989, PMID:2678100). Endothelin-1 acts as an endogenous pain mediator, sensitizing nociceptors through activation of ETA and ETB receptors, and these neurons are implicated in vascular pain signalling. EDN1-expressing DRG neurons have been characterized in rat; their prevalence and properties in human DRG remain to be systematically determined, as EDN1 is not yet represented in human DRG single-cell transcriptomic datasets."^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string)

- [cervical dorsal root ganglion peripherin neuron](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4079004) [definition](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/IAO_0000115) "A small-diameter sensory neuron whose soma is located in the cervical dorsal root ganglion and that expresses peripherin (encoded by PRPH), a type III intermediate filament protein. This neuron is unmyelinated, conducts action potentials as a C-fiber, and encompasses nociceptive and thermoceptive functional subpopulations. In human DRG, peripherin-immunoreactive neurons are predominantly of small diameter (Chang et al. 2018, PMID:28424991), distinguishing them from large-diameter myelinated A-fiber neurons that instead express neurofilament heavy chain (Haberberger et al. 2019, PMID:31293388). In mice, peripherin similarly marks unmyelinated primary afferent neurons."^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 
  - [database_cross_reference](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref) "10.1007/s12264-017-0132-3"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string)

- [cervical dorsal root ganglion substance P neuron](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4079007) [definition](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/IAO_0000115) "A peptidergic nociceptor whose soma is located in the cervical dorsal root ganglion and that expresses substance P, an 11-amino-acid neuropeptide cleaved from protachykinin-1 (encoded by TAC1). This small-diameter neuron frequently co-expresses CGRP and belongs to the TrkA-positive peptidergic population. Upon nociceptive activation, it releases substance P both centrally in the spinal cord dorsal horn and peripherally at sensory nerve terminals, mediating neurogenic inflammation through NK1 receptor signalling (Haberberger et al. 2019, PMID:31293388). Substance P-immunoreactive neurons have been consistently identified in human DRG by immunohistochemistry across multiple studies."^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 
  - [database_cross_reference](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref) "PMID:31293388"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string)

- [ciliary ganglion VIP/PHI neuron](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4033139) [definition](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/IAO_0000115) "A parasympathetic postganglionic neuron whose soma is located in the ciliary ganglion and that co-expresses vasoactive intestinal peptide (VIP) and peptide histidine isoleucine (PHI, both encoded by the VIP gene). This neuron provides parasympathetic innervation to the eye, contributing to regulation of pupillary constriction and ciliary muscle accommodation. It has been identified in human ciliary ganglia by immunohistochemistry (Kiyokawa et al. 2012, PMID:22095632). VIP/PHI co-expression distinguishes this subpopulation from other cholinergic parasympathetic neurons in the ciliary ganglion and is characteristic of a subset of cranial parasympathetic neurons in humans and other mammals."^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string)

- [deep zone articular chondrocyte](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_0020039) [date](http://purl.org/dc/terms/date) "2026-02-18T11:06:13Z"^^[dateTime](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#dateTime) 

- [deep zone articular chondrocyte](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_0020039) [id](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#id) "CL:0020039"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

- [deep zone articular chondrocyte](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_0020039) [has_related_synonym](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasRelatedSynonym) "radial zone articular chondrocyte"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 
  - [database_cross_reference](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref) "PMID:23015907"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

- [deep zone articular chondrocyte](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_0020039) [definition](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/IAO_0000115) "An articular chondrocyte located in the deep (radial) zone of articular cartilage, characterized by columnar arrangement perpendicular to the joint surface and residence within a matrix containing the highest proteoglycan concentration and large-diameter collagen fibrils oriented radially. In humans, this cell expresses collagen type X (COL10A1) and provides maximal resistance to compressive forces. It is positioned adjacent to the tidemark, where collagen fibrils extend into the calcified cartilage to anchor the articular cartilage to subchondral bone."^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 
  - [database_cross_reference](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref) "PMID:41226342"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

  - [database_cross_reference](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref) "PMID:23015907"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

  - [database_cross_reference](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref) "PMID:23124445"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

- [deep zone articular chondrocyte](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_0020039) [label](http://www.w3.org/2000/01/rdf-schema#label) "deep zone articular chondrocyte"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string)

- [fasciacyte](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_0020043) [definition](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/IAO_0000115) "A mesenchymal stromal cell of the deep fascia (e.g., fascia lata) that is vimentin-positive, CD68-negative, and S-100A4-positive, organized in small clusters at the interface between fibrous fascial sublayers and loose connective tissue. It is specialized for hyaluronan-rich ECM biosynthesis, as evidenced by HAS2 mRNA expression, Alcian Blue staining, and anti-HABP immunoreactivity, and functions to regulate fascial gliding and viscoelasticity."^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string)

- [fasciacyte](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_0020043) [comment](http://www.w3.org/2000/01/rdf-schema#comment) "Stecco et al. demonstrate that fasciacytes differ from classical fascial fibroblasts in morphology, location (small clusters at the interface between fibrous and loose fascial layers), marker profile (S-100A4 expression), and ECM output (HA-rich rather than collagen-rich)."^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

- [fasciacyte](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_0020043) [label](http://www.w3.org/2000/01/rdf-schema#label) "fasciacyte"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string)

- [hybrid osteochondral skeletal cell](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_0020028) [contributor](http://purl.org/dc/terms/contributor) [0009-0000-8480-9277](https://orcid.org/0009-0000-8480-9277) 

- [hybrid osteochondral skeletal cell](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_0020028) [creator](http://purl.org/dc/terms/creator) "GitHub Copilot"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

- [hybrid osteochondral skeletal cell](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_0020028) [date](http://purl.org/dc/terms/date) "2025-12-16T14:37:04Z"^^[dateTime](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#dateTime) 

- [hybrid osteochondral skeletal cell](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_0020028) [id](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#id) "CL:0020028"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

- [hybrid osteochondral skeletal cell](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_0020028) [definition](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/IAO_0000115) "A skeletal cell at the periosteal surface of the murine rib that displays hybrid osteochondral properties, emerging within the large callus that bridges segmental rib defects. It derives from a Sox9-expressing periosteal skeletal stem/progenitor subpopulation that constitutes only a small fraction of uninjured rib periosteum. After injury, these cells populate the callus and co-express cartilage and bone regulators Sox9 and Runx2, as well as matrix genes Col2a1 and Col1a1, while exhibiting dual chondrocyte/osteoblast properties."^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 
  - [database_cross_reference](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref) "PMID:30983567"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

- [hybrid osteochondral skeletal cell](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_0020028) [label](http://www.w3.org/2000/01/rdf-schema#label) "hybrid osteochondral skeletal cell"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

- [hybrid osteochondral skeletal cell](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_0020028) SubClassOf [bone cell](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_0001035) 

- [hybrid osteochondral skeletal cell](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_0020028) SubClassOf [skeletogenic cell](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_0007001) 

- [hybrid osteochondral skeletal cell](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_0020028) SubClassOf [BFO_0000050](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/BFO_0000050) some [UBERON_0002515](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/UBERON_0002515) 

- [hybrid osteochondral skeletal cell](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_0020028) SubClassOf [RO_0002162](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/RO_0002162) some [NCBITaxon_10090](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/NCBITaxon_10090)

- [intestinofugal neuron](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_0020049) [definition](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/IAO_0000115) "An enteric neuron whose soma resides in the myenteric plexus of the intestine and whose axon projects outside the gut wall to synapse on neurons in prevertebral sympathetic ganglia (celiac, superior mesenteric, or inferior mesenteric ganglia). This neuron provides a pathway for gut-to-brain communication via sympathetic prevertebral ganglia. In humans, 89% are immunopositive for choline acetyltransferase (ChAT); CART (cocaine- and amphetamine-regulated transcript) is NOT a human marker (0% CART+) but is present in rodent viscerofugal neurons."^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string)

- [intraepithelial lymphocyte](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_0002496) [definition](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/IAO_0000115) "A tissue-resident lymphocyte located within the epithelial layer of mucosal tissues, particularly within the gastrointestinal, respiratory, and reproductive tracts. Characterised by permanent residency, this cell typically expresses CD103 (integrin alpha-E), which binds to E-cadherin on epithelial cells, enabling epithelial retention in both mice and humans. Phenotypically, IEL displays an activated, antigen-experienced state characterised by the constitutive expression of cytotoxic molecules (granzyme B, perforin) and innate-like receptors (such as NKG2D), enabling rapid, localised surveillance and immediate response to epithelial stress."^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 
  - [database_cross_reference](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref) "PMID:29674648"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

  - [database_cross_reference](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref) "WIKIPEDIA:Intraepithelial_lymphocyte"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

  - [database_cross_reference](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref) "MP:0008894"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string)

- [intrinsic cardiac ganglion TH neuron](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4079010) [definition](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/IAO_0000115) "A catecholaminergic neuron whose soma is located in an intrinsic cardiac ganglion and that expresses tyrosine hydroxylase (TH, encoded by TH), the rate-limiting enzyme in catecholamine biosynthesis. This neuron constitutes a minor subpopulation within the predominantly cholinergic parasympathetic intrinsic cardiac nervous system, identified in adult human cardiac ganglia by immunohistochemistry (Singh et al. 1999, PMID:9918529; Kawano et al. 2003, DOI:10.1007/s003800300005). It participates in local cardiac autonomic regulation, including modulation of heart rate and contractility. Its catecholaminergic phenotype distinguishes it from the majority cholinergic neurons of the same ganglia."^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string)

- [lumbar dorsal root ganglion CGRP neuron](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4079011) [date](http://purl.org/dc/terms/date) "2026-03-13T11:13:54Z"^^[dateTime](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#dateTime) 

- [lumbar dorsal root ganglion CGRP neuron](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4079011) [has_related_synonym](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasRelatedSynonym) "peptidergic nociceptor"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

- [lumbar dorsal root ganglion CGRP neuron](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4079011) [id](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#id) "CL:4079011"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

- [lumbar dorsal root ganglion CGRP neuron](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4079011) [definition](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/IAO_0000115) "A peptidergic nociceptor whose soma is located in the lumbar dorsal root ganglion, characterized by expression of calcitonin gene-related peptide (CGRP, encoded by CALCA). This small- to medium-diameter neuron belongs to the TrkA-positive peptidergic subpopulation and typically co-expresses substance P. It innervates peripheral tissues including skin and viscera, where it mediates neurogenic inflammation and nociceptive signalling through release of CGRP from peripheral terminals during tissue injury (Haberberger et al. 2019, PMID:31293388). In human DRG, CGRP-immunoreactive neurons represent a substantial proportion of nociceptors, comparable to the pattern observed in rodents (Rostock et al. 2018, PMID:29229553)."^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 
  - [database_cross_reference](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref) "PMID:29229553"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

  - [database_cross_reference](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref) "PMID:31293388"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

  - [database_cross_reference](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref) "10.1016/S0304-3940(00)00772-2"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string)

### lumbar dorsal root ganglion Nav1.7 neuron `http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4079013`

#### Added
- Class: [lumbar dorsal root ganglion Nav1.7 neuron](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4079013) 

- [lumbar dorsal root ganglion Nav1.7 neuron](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4079013) [contributor](http://purl.org/dc/terms/contributor) [0000-0001-6677-8489](https://orcid.org/0000-0001-6677-8489) 

- [lumbar dorsal root ganglion Nav1.7 neuron](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4079013) [date](http://purl.org/dc/terms/date) "2026-03-13T11:13:54Z"^^[dateTime](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#dateTime) 

- [lumbar dorsal root ganglion Nav1.7 neuron](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4079013) [id](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#id) "CL:4079013"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

- [lumbar dorsal root ganglion Nav1.7 neuron](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4079013) [definition](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/IAO_0000115) "A nociceptor whose soma is located in the lumbar dorsal root ganglion and that expresses the voltage-gated sodium channel Nav1.7 (encoded by SCN9A). This neuron is characterized by Nav1.7-dependent action potential initiation and amplification, which is essential for normal pain sensation in humans. Nav1.7 contributes approximately 50% of total sodium channel current in human DRG nociceptors (Chang et al. 2018, PMID:28424991). In human DRG, Nav1.7 immunoreactivity is detected in 54-57% of TrkA-positive neurons (Rostock et al. 2018, PMID:29229553). Human genetic evidence confirms Nav1.7 as necessary and sufficient for nociceptive function in these neurons."^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 
  - [database_cross_reference](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref) "10.1038/nn.3602"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

  - [database_cross_reference](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref) "10.1007/s12264-017-0132-3"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

  - [database_cross_reference](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref) "PMID:29229553"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string)

- [lumbar dorsal root ganglion Nav1.9 neuron](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4079014) [definition](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/IAO_0000115) "A nociceptor whose soma is located in the lumbar dorsal root ganglion and that expresses the voltage-gated sodium channel Nav1.9 (encoded by SCN11A). This neuron is characterized by a persistent, tetrodotoxin-resistant sodium current that modulates resting membrane potential and amplifies subthreshold depolarizations, contributing to enhanced excitability during inflammation (Dib-Hajj et al. 2002, PMID:11972962). In human DRG, Nav1.9-immunoreactive neurons constitute approximately 26% of TrkA-positive neurons, a significantly higher proportion than the 12% observed in mouse (Rostock et al. 2018, PMID:29229553), suggesting species differences in inflammatory pain processing."^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string)

- [lumbar dorsal root ganglion Piezo2 neuron](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4079016) [definition](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/IAO_0000115) "A mechanosensitive sensory neuron whose soma is located in the lumbar dorsal root ganglion and that expresses the mechanically activated ion channel Piezo2 (encoded by PIEZO2). This neuron transduces mechanical stimuli and is involved in light touch perception and proprioception. In human DRG, Piezo2-immunoreactive neurons constitute approximately 35% of TrkA-positive neurons, compared to 26% in mouse (Rostock et al. 2018, PMID:29229553). This subpopulation includes both low-threshold mechanoreceptors mediating innocuous touch and a subset of mechanically sensitive nociceptors, reflecting the dual role of Piezo2 in somatosensation across species."^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string)

- [lumbar dorsal root ganglion RET neuron](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4079017) [definition](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/IAO_0000115) "A non-peptidergic nociceptor whose soma is located in the lumbar dorsal root ganglion and that expresses the receptor tyrosine kinase RET (encoded by RET). This neuron is distinguished from peptidergic nociceptors by its dependence on glial cell-derived neurotrophic factor family ligands rather than nerve growth factor, and in rodents it characteristically binds isolectin B4. In human DRG, RET-immunoreactive neurons constitute approximately 46% of TrkA-positive neurons, a significantly higher proportion than the 23% observed in mouse (Rostock et al. 2018, PMID:29229553), indicating an expanded non-peptidergic nociceptor compartment in humans."^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string)

- [lumbar dorsal root ganglion TRPV1 neuron](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4079019) [definition](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/IAO_0000115) "A polymodal nociceptor whose soma is located in the lumbar dorsal root ganglion and that expresses the transient receptor potential vanilloid 1 channel (TRPV1, encoded by TRPV1). This neuron detects noxious heat above 43 degrees Celsius, protons, and endogenous lipid mediators, and is activated by capsaicin. In human DRG, TRPV1-immunoreactive neurons constitute approximately 54% of TrkA-positive neurons, significantly higher than the 35% observed in mouse (Rostock et al. 2018, PMID:29229553). These neurons are predominantly small-diameter nociceptors that innervate skin and visceral organs, where they function as primary detectors of thermal and chemical noxious stimuli."^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string)

- [lumbar dorsal root ganglion endothelin-1 neuron](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4079012) [definition](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/IAO_0000115) "A sensory neuron whose soma is located in the lumbar dorsal root ganglion and that expresses endothelin-1 (EDN1). In rat DRG, EDN1 immunoreactivity has been detected in a subset of neuron somata (Giaid et al. 1989, PMID:2678100). Endothelin-1 acts as an endogenous pain mediator, sensitizing nociceptors through activation of ETA and ETB receptors, and these neurons are implicated in vascular pain signalling. EDN1-expressing DRG neurons have been characterized in rat; their prevalence and properties in human DRG remain to be systematically determined, as EDN1 is not yet represented in human DRG single-cell transcriptomic datasets."^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string)

- [lumbar dorsal root ganglion peripherin neuron](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4079015) [definition](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/IAO_0000115) "A small-diameter sensory neuron whose soma is located in the lumbar dorsal root ganglion and that expresses peripherin (encoded by PRPH), a type III intermediate filament protein. This neuron is unmyelinated, conducts action potentials as a C-fiber, and encompasses nociceptive and thermoceptive functional subpopulations. In human DRG, peripherin-immunoreactive neurons are predominantly of small diameter (Chang et al. 2018, PMID:28424991), distinguishing them from large-diameter myelinated A-fiber neurons that instead express neurofilament heavy chain (Haberberger et al. 2019, PMID:31293388). In mice, peripherin similarly marks unmyelinated primary afferent neurons."^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string)

- [lumbar dorsal root ganglion substance P neuron](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4079018) [definition](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/IAO_0000115) "A peptidergic nociceptor whose soma is located in the lumbar dorsal root ganglion and that expresses substance P, an 11-amino-acid neuropeptide cleaved from protachykinin-1 (encoded by TAC1). This small-diameter neuron frequently co-expresses CGRP and belongs to the TrkA-positive peptidergic population. Upon nociceptive activation, it releases substance P both centrally in the spinal cord dorsal horn and peripherally at sensory nerve terminals, mediating neurogenic inflammation through NK1 receptor signalling (Haberberger et al. 2019, PMID:31293388). Substance P-immunoreactive neurons have been consistently identified in human DRG by immunohistochemistry across multiple studies."^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 
  - [database_cross_reference](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref) "PMID:31293388"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

  - [database_cross_reference](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref) "10.1016/S0304-3940(00)00772-2"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string)

- [sacral dorsal root ganglion CGRP neuron](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4079020) [definition](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/IAO_0000115) "A peptidergic nociceptor whose soma is located in the sacral dorsal root ganglion, characterized by expression of calcitonin gene-related peptide (CGRP, encoded by CALCA). This small- to medium-diameter neuron belongs to the TrkA-positive peptidergic subpopulation and typically co-expresses substance P. It innervates peripheral tissues including skin and viscera, where it mediates neurogenic inflammation and nociceptive signalling through release of CGRP from peripheral terminals during tissue injury (Haberberger et al. 2019, PMID:31293388). - [sacral dorsal root ganglion Nav1.7 neuron](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4079022) [contributor](http://purl.org/dc/terms/contributor) [0000-0001-6677-8489](https://orcid.org/0000-0001-6677-8489) 

- [sacral dorsal root ganglion Nav1.7 neuron](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4079022) [date](http://purl.org/dc/terms/date) "2026-03-13T11:13:54Z"^^[dateTime](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#dateTime) 

- [sacral dorsal root ganglion Nav1.7 neuron](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4079022) [id](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#id) "CL:4079022"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

- [sacral dorsal root ganglion Nav1.7 neuron](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4079022) [definition](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/IAO_0000115) "A nociceptor whose soma is located in the sacral dorsal root ganglion and that expresses the voltage-gated sodium channel Nav1.7 (encoded by SCN9A). This neuron is characterized by Nav1.7-dependent action potential initiation and amplification, which is essential for normal pain sensation in humans. Nav1.7 contributes approximately 50% of total sodium channel current in human DRG nociceptors (Chang et al. 2018, PMID:28424991). In human DRG, Nav1.7 immunoreactivity is detected in 54-57% of TrkA-positive neurons (Rostock et al. 2018, PMID:29229553). Human genetic evidence confirms Nav1.7 as necessary and sufficient for nociceptive function in these neurons."^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string)

- [sacral dorsal root ganglion Nav1.9 neuron](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4079023) [definition](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/IAO_0000115) "A nociceptor whose soma is located in the sacral dorsal root ganglion and that expresses the voltage-gated sodium channel Nav1.9 (encoded by SCN11A). This neuron is characterized by a persistent, tetrodotoxin-resistant sodium current that modulates resting membrane potential and amplifies subthreshold depolarizations, contributing to enhanced excitability during inflammation (Dib-Hajj et al. 2002, PMID:11972962). In human DRG, Nav1.9-immunoreactive neurons constitute approximately 26% of TrkA-positive neurons, a significantly higher proportion than the 12% observed in mouse (Rostock et al. 2018, PMID:29229553), suggesting species differences in inflammatory pain processing."^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string)

- [sacral dorsal root ganglion Piezo2 neuron](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4079025) [definition](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/IAO_0000115) "A mechanosensitive sensory neuron whose soma is located in the sacral dorsal root ganglion and that expresses the mechanically activated ion channel Piezo2 (encoded by PIEZO2). This neuron transduces mechanical stimuli and is involved in light touch perception and proprioception. In human DRG, Piezo2-immunoreactive neurons constitute approximately 35% of TrkA-positive neurons, compared to 26% in mouse (Rostock et al. 2018, PMID:29229553). This subpopulation includes both low-threshold mechanoreceptors mediating innocuous touch and a subset of mechanically sensitive nociceptors, reflecting the dual role of Piezo2 in somatosensation across species."^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string)

- [sacral dorsal root ganglion TRPV1 neuron](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4079028) [definition](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/IAO_0000115) "A polymodal nociceptor whose soma is located in the sacral dorsal root ganglion and that expresses the transient receptor potential vanilloid 1 channel (TRPV1, encoded by TRPV1). This neuron detects noxious heat above 43 degrees Celsius, protons, and endogenous lipid mediators, and is activated by capsaicin. In human DRG, TRPV1-immunoreactive neurons constitute approximately 54% of TrkA-positive neurons, significantly higher than the 35% observed in mouse (Rostock et al. 2018, PMID:29229553). These neurons are predominantly small-diameter nociceptors that innervate skin and visceral organs, where they function as primary detectors of thermal and chemical noxious stimuli."^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string)

- [sacral dorsal root ganglion endothelin-1 neuron](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4079021) [date](http://purl.org/dc/terms/date) "2026-03-13T11:13:54Z"^^[dateTime](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#dateTime) 

- [sacral dorsal root ganglion endothelin-1 neuron](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4079021) [has_exact_synonym](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasExactSynonym) "sacral dorsal root ganglion Endothelin 1 neuron"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

- [sacral dorsal root ganglion endothelin-1 neuron](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4079021) [has_related_synonym](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasRelatedSynonym) "EDN1 neuron"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

- [sacral dorsal root ganglion endothelin-1 neuron](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4079021) [id](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#id) "CL:4079021"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

- [sacral dorsal root ganglion endothelin-1 neuron](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4079021) [definition](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/IAO_0000115) "A sensory neuron whose soma is located in the sacral dorsal root ganglion and that expresses endothelin-1 (EDN1). In rat DRG, EDN1 immunoreactivity has been detected in a subset of neuron somata (Giaid et al. 1989, PMID:2678100). Endothelin-1 acts as an endogenous pain mediator, sensitizing nociceptors through activation of ETA and ETB receptors, and these neurons are implicated in vascular pain signalling. EDN1-expressing DRG neurons have been characterized in rat; their prevalence and properties in human DRG remain to be systematically determined, as EDN1 is not yet represented in human DRG single-cell transcriptomic datasets."^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 
  - [database_cross_reference](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref) "10.1073/pnas.86.19.7634"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

- [sacral dorsal root ganglion endothelin-1 neuron](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4079021) [label](http://www.w3.org/2000/01/rdf-schema#label) "sacral dorsal root ganglion endothelin-1 neuron"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

- [sacral dorsal root ganglion endothelin-1 neuron](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4079021) SubClassOf [BFO_0000002](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/BFO_0000002)

- [sacral dorsal root ganglion peripherin neuron](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4079024) [definition](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/IAO_0000115) "A small-diameter sensory neuron whose soma is located in the sacral dorsal root ganglion and that expresses peripherin (encoded by PRPH), a type III intermediate filament protein. This neuron is unmyelinated, conducts action potentials as a C-fiber, and encompasses nociceptive and thermoceptive functional subpopulations. In human DRG, peripherin-immunoreactive neurons are predominantly of small diameter (Chang et al. 2018, PMID:28424991), distinguishing them from large-diameter myelinated A-fiber neurons that instead express neurofilament heavy chain (Haberberger et al. 2019, PMID:31293388). In mice, peripherin similarly marks unmyelinated primary afferent neurons."^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 
  - [database_cross_reference](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref) "10.1007/s12264-017-0132-3"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string)

- [sacral dorsal root ganglion substance P neuron](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4079027) [definition](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/IAO_0000115) "A peptidergic nociceptor whose soma is located in the sacral dorsal root ganglion and that expresses substance P, an 11-amino-acid neuropeptide cleaved from protachykinin-1 (encoded by TAC1). This small-diameter neuron frequently co-expresses CGRP and belongs to the TrkA-positive peptidergic population. Upon nociceptive activation, it releases substance P both centrally in the spinal cord dorsal horn and peripherally at sensory nerve terminals, mediating neurogenic inflammation through NK1 receptor signalling (Haberberger et al. 2019, PMID:31293388). Substance P-immunoreactive neurons have been consistently identified in human DRG by immunohistochemistry across multiple studies."^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 
  - [database_cross_reference](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref) "PMID:31293388"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string)

- [secretomotor/vasodilator neuron of myenteric plexus](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_0020048) [definition](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/IAO_0000115) "An enteric neuron whose soma resides in the myenteric plexus and which controls mucosal secretion and blood flow by innervating secretory epithelia and submucosal blood vessels. This neuron is characterised by expression of vasoactive intestinal peptide (VIP). In mouse, two Glp2r+ subtypes have been identified: PSVN1 (VIP+, non-cholinergic) and PSVN2 (ChAT+, cholinergic). In human, only the VIP+ non-cholinergic subtype has been detected."^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string)

- [superficial zone articular chondrocyte](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_0020037) [definition](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/IAO_0000115) "An articular chondrocyte located in the most superficial zone of articular cartilage, characterized by flattened morphology and tangential alignment parallel to the joint surface, and residing within a matrix of fine collagen fibrils and relatively low proteoglycan content. In mice and humans, this cell typically expresses lubricin (PRG4) and contributes to lubrication and resistance to shear and tensile forces at the cartilage surface."^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string)

- [thoracic dorsal root ganglion CGRP neuron](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4079029) [definition](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/IAO_0000115) "A peptidergic nociceptor whose soma is located in the thoracic dorsal root ganglion, characterized by expression of calcitonin gene-related peptide (CGRP, encoded by CALCA). This small- to medium-diameter neuron belongs to the TrkA-positive peptidergic subpopulation and typically co-expresses substance P. It innervates peripheral tissues including skin and viscera, where it mediates neurogenic inflammation and nociceptive signalling through release of CGRP from peripheral terminals during tissue injury (Haberberger et al. 2019, PMID:31293388). In human DRG, CGRP-immunoreactive neurons represent a substantial proportion of nociceptors, comparable to the pattern observed in rodents (Rostock et al. 2018, PMID:29229553)."^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string)

### thoracic dorsal root ganglion Nav1.7 neuron `http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4079031`

#### Added
- Class: [thoracic dorsal root ganglion Nav1.7 neuron](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4079031) 

- [thoracic dorsal root ganglion Nav1.7 neuron](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4079031) [contributor](http://purl.org/dc/terms/contributor) [0000-0001-6677-8489](https://orcid.org/0000-0001-6677-8489) 

- [thoracic dorsal root ganglion Nav1.7 neuron](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4079031) [date](http://purl.org/dc/terms/date) "2026-03-13T11:13:54Z"^^[dateTime](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#dateTime) 

- [thoracic dorsal root ganglion Nav1.7 neuron](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4079031) [id](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#id) "CL:4079031"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

- [thoracic dorsal root ganglion Nav1.7 neuron](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4079031) [definition](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/IAO_0000115) "A nociceptor whose soma is located in the thoracic dorsal root ganglion and that expresses the voltage-gated sodium channel Nav1.7 (encoded by SCN9A). This neuron is characterized by Nav1.7-dependent action potential initiation and amplification, which is essential for normal pain sensation in humans. Nav1.7 contributes approximately 50% of total sodium channel current in human DRG nociceptors (Chang et al. 2018, PMID:28424991). In human DRG, Nav1.7 immunoreactivity is detected in 54-57% of TrkA-positive neurons (Rostock et al. 2018, PMID:29229553). Human genetic evidence confirms Nav1.7 as necessary and sufficient for nociceptive function in these neurons."^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 
  - [database_cross_reference](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref) "10.1038/nn.3602"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string)

- [thoracic dorsal root ganglion Nav1.9 neuron](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4079032) [definition](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/IAO_0000115) "A nociceptor whose soma is located in the thoracic dorsal root ganglion and that expresses the voltage-gated sodium channel Nav1.9 (encoded by SCN11A). This neuron is characterized by a persistent, tetrodotoxin-resistant sodium current that modulates resting membrane potential and amplifies subthreshold depolarizations, contributing to enhanced excitability during inflammation (Dib-Hajj et al. 2002, PMID:11972962). In human DRG, Nav1.9-immunoreactive neurons constitute approximately 26% of TrkA-positive neurons, a significantly higher proportion than the 12% observed in mouse (Rostock et al. 2018, PMID:29229553), suggesting species differences in inflammatory pain processing."^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string)

- [thoracic dorsal root ganglion Piezo2 neuron](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4079034) [definition](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/IAO_0000115) "A mechanosensitive sensory neuron whose soma is located in the thoracic dorsal root ganglion and that expresses the mechanically activated ion channel Piezo2 (encoded by PIEZO2). This neuron transduces mechanical stimuli and is involved in light touch perception and proprioception. In human DRG, Piezo2-immunoreactive neurons constitute approximately 35% of TrkA-positive neurons, compared to 26% in mouse (Rostock et al. 2018, PMID:29229553). This subpopulation includes both low-threshold mechanoreceptors mediating innocuous touch and a subset of mechanically sensitive nociceptors, reflecting the dual role of Piezo2 in somatosensation across species."^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string)

This neuron is distinguished from peptidergic nociceptors by its dependence on glial cell-derived neurotrophic factor family ligands rather than nerve growth factor, and in rodents it characteristically binds isolectin B4. - [thoracic dorsal root ganglion TRPV1 neuron](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4079037) [definition](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/IAO_0000115) "A polymodal nociceptor whose soma is located in the thoracic dorsal root ganglion and that expresses the transient receptor potential vanilloid 1 channel (TRPV1, encoded by TRPV1). This neuron detects noxious heat above 43 degrees Celsius, protons, and endogenous lipid mediators, and is activated by capsaicin. In human DRG, TRPV1-immunoreactive neurons constitute approximately 54% of TrkA-positive neurons, significantly higher than the 35% observed in mouse (Rostock et al. 2018, PMID:29229553). These neurons are predominantly small-diameter nociceptors that innervate skin and visceral organs, where they function as primary detectors of thermal and chemical noxious stimuli."^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string)

- [thoracic dorsal root ganglion endothelin-1 neuron](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4079030) [definition](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/IAO_0000115) "A sensory neuron whose soma is located in the thoracic dorsal root ganglion and that expresses endothelin-1 (EDN1). In rat DRG, EDN1 immunoreactivity has been detected in a subset of neuron somata (Giaid et al. 1989, PMID:2678100). Endothelin-1 acts as an endogenous pain mediator, sensitizing nociceptors through activation of ETA and ETB receptors, and these neurons are implicated in vascular pain signalling. EDN1-expressing DRG neurons have been characterized in rat; their prevalence and properties in human DRG remain to be systematically determined, as EDN1 is not yet represented in human DRG single-cell transcriptomic datasets."^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 
  - [database_cross_reference](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref) "10.1073/pnas.86.19.7634"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string)

- [thoracic dorsal root ganglion peripherin neuron](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4079033) [definition](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/IAO_0000115) "A small-diameter sensory neuron whose soma is located in the thoracic dorsal root ganglion and that expresses peripherin (encoded by PRPH), a type III intermediate filament protein. This neuron is unmyelinated, conducts action potentials as a C-fiber, and encompasses nociceptive and thermoceptive functional subpopulations. In human DRG, peripherin-immunoreactive neurons are predominantly of small diameter (Chang et al. 2018, PMID:28424991), distinguishing them from large-diameter myelinated A-fiber neurons that instead express neurofilament heavy chain (Haberberger et al. 2019, PMID:31293388). In mice, peripherin similarly marks unmyelinated primary afferent neurons."^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string)

- [thoracic dorsal root ganglion substance P neuron](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4079036) [definition](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/IAO_0000115) "A peptidergic nociceptor whose soma is located in the thoracic dorsal root ganglion and that expresses substance P, an 11-amino-acid neuropeptide cleaved from protachykinin-1 (encoded by TAC1). This small-diameter neuron frequently co-expresses CGRP and belongs to the TrkA-positive peptidergic population. Upon nociceptive activation, it releases substance P both centrally in the spinal cord dorsal horn and peripherally at sensory nerve terminals, mediating neurogenic inflammation through NK1 receptor signalling (Haberberger et al. 2019, PMID:31293388). Substance P-immunoreactive neurons have been consistently identified in human DRG by immunohistochemistry across multiple studies."^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string)

- [type IV spiral ligament fibrocyte](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_0002668) [definition](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/IAO_0000115) "A spiral ligament fibrocyte that is located in the triangular space inferior to the crista basilaris (basilar crest). This cell is spindle-shaped and expresses NKCC1 but minimal to no Na,K-ATPase (ATP1A1, ATP1B1) in mice and humans, and lacks connexin 26/30 in mice, indicating it does not participate in K⁺ recycling, unlike type II fibrocytes. Type IV fibrocyte is uniquely characterised by strong expression of connective tissue growth factor (CTGF) in mice, suggesting roles in tissue remodelling and paracrine signalling to other cochlear cells."^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string)

- [type V spiral ligament fibrocyte](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_0002667) [definition](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/IAO_0000115) "A spiral ligament fibrocyte located in the suprastrial region above the stria vascularis, distinguished from other fibrocytes by their unique expression of COX-1 in guinea pigs and end-foot structures that directly contact capillaries (Dai and Shi, 2011). This fibro-vascular coupling enables type V fibrocytes to regulate cochlear blood flow by translating Ca&sup2;⁺ signals into capillary vasodilation via COX-1-derived prostaglandins. This cell also participates in K⁺ recycling, expressing Na,K-ATPase (ATP1A1, ATP1B1) in mice and humans, and connexin 26/30 gap junctions enabling intercellular K⁺ transport within the spiral ligament syncytium (Peeleman et al., 2020)."^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string)
